HD Press Release: Decision from the Danish FSA regarding Danske Bank 's management and governance in relation to the matter concerning its branch in Estonia
WC 784 words
PD 3 May 2018
ET 03:01
SN Dow Jones Institutional News
SC DJDN
LA English
CY Copyright 2018, Dow Jones & Company, Inc.

LP 

TD 

 
 
 
 
 
 
                                      Holmens Kanal 2 -- 12 
  Company announcement No. 31/2018     DK-1092 Kbenhavn K 
                                       Tel. +45 45 14 56 95 
                                       3 May 2018 
 
   Decision from the Danish FSA  regarding Danske Bank 's management and 
governance 
 
   in relation to the matter concerning its branch in Estonia 
 
   The Danish FSA  has assessed the role of Danske Bank 's management and 
senior employees in the matter relating to the now closed down 
non-resident portfolio at Danske Bank 's branch in Estonia. The 
assessment gives rise to eight orders and eight reprimands. Danske Bank  
has taken note of the orders and reprimands. In addition to the 
initiatives already taken in recent years, Danske Bank  will now launch 
further measures to ensure that it complies with all orders. 
 
   "We take the criticism expressed by the FSA very seriously," says Thomas 
F. Borgen , CEO. "We agree that we should have understood the depth and 
scope of the problems in Estonia at an earlier stage and should have 
reacted faster and more forcefully. As the FSA's decision states, 
beginning in 2014, we took a number of initiatives to reduce the risk 
and improve controls. But today, it is also clear that we did too little 
too slowly. There is unfortunately nothing we can do to change that. 
Instead, we need to ensure that it cannot happen again. That is one of 
the reasons why we launched thorough investigations in autumn 2017." 
 
   The wording of the orders and reprimands is given in the FSA's decision 
document 'Danske Bank 's management and governance in relation to the AML 
case at the Estonian branch' of 3 May 2018, which is enclosed with this 
company announcement. 
 
   Anti-money laundering measures 
 
   The non-resident portfolio in Estonia, to which the problems relate, has 
been closed down, and in recent years, Danske Bank  has invested 
massively in compliance activities: 
 
   "As the FSA also states, we have strengthened our AML efforts in recent 
years," says Thomas F. Borgen . "Today, Danske Bank  has more than 900 
employees working to combat financial crime. Our governance and control 
functions have been significantly strengthened and we have made 
considerable IT investments and have strengthened competencies in a 
number of support functions. Today, the situation is quite different 
from what it was at the time. So we believe that we have come a long way 
towards addressing the issues covered by the orders. Now we need to work 
resolutely and systematically to ensure that we comply with all orders." 
 
   Moreover, after the organisational changes announced on 6 April this 
year, the Compliance unit reports directly to the CEO. 
 
   Order to reassess the solvency need 
 
   Among other things, the Danish FSA  orders the Board of Directors and the 
Executive Board to reassess the bank's and the banking group's solvency 
need in order to ensure an adequate internal capital coverage of 
compliance and reputational risks as a result of weaknesses in the 
bank's governance. The FSA initially estimates that a Pillar II add-on 
should amount to at least DKK 5 billion, or about 0.7% of the REA (risk 
exposure amount) at the end of 2017. An add-on of DKK 5 billion will 
increase the Group's solvency need from 10.5% to 11.2% calculated at 31 
March 2018. The increased solvency need should be viewed in light of a 
total capital ratio of 21.4% at 31 March 2018. The Group will thus 
continue to have a considerable solvency buffer. 
 
   Ongoing investigations 
 
   Danske Bank  earlier concluded that, in the period from 2007 to 2015, it 
was not sufficiently effective in preventing the branch in Estonia from 
potentially being used for money laundering and that this was due to 
critical deficiencies in governance and controls. As a result, 
comprehensive investigations into conditions at the Estonian branch 
during the period in question were launched in the autumn of 2017. The 
investigations focus on two separate things: A thorough review of 
customers and transactions during the period, and an examination of the 
course of events, including whether managers and employees lived up to 
their responsibilities to a sufficient degree. The investigations are 
expected to be completed in September 2018 at the latest. 
 
   Danske Bank  
 
   Contact: Kenni Leth, Group Press Officer, tel. +45 45 14 14 00

HD Press Release: S&PGRBulletin: Dankse Bank Rtgs Unaffctd By FAS Orders For Now
WC 1209 words
PD 4 May 2018
ET 11:40
SN Dow Jones Institutional News
SC DJDN
LA English
CY Copyright 2018, Dow Jones & Company, Inc.

LP 

TD 

 
 
The following is a press release from S&P Global Ratings: 
 
MOSCOW (S&P Global Ratings) May 4, 2018--S&P Global Ratings said today that 
its ratings on Danske Bank A/S  (A/Positive/A-1) are not immediately affected 
by Danish Financial Supervisory Authority  (Danish FSA ; Finanstilsynet) orders 
regarding the anti-money laundering (AML) case at the bank's Estonian branch. 
 
On May 3, 2018, the Danish FSA  published a report assessing the role of Danske 
Bank 's management and senior employees in the AML case at the bank's Estonian 
branch. 
 
The publication refers to deficiencies in AML activities in the branch between 
2011-2013, and contains a number of reprimands and orders. 
 
As one of the measures aimed at improving governance, the Danish FSA  will 
assess how much of a Pillar II capital increase in solvency is necessary by 
considering compliance and reputational risks. As a first estimate, they will 
require an add-on of Danish krone (DKK) 5 billion (EUR671 million), equivalent 
to approximately 0.7% of the risk exposure amount at the end of 2017. An 
add-on of DKK5 billion will increase Danske Bank 's common equity tier 1 
capital requirement to 11.2% from 10.5% calculated at March 31, 2018, as 
compared with a total capital ratio of 21.4% at March 31,2018. 
 
We see no immediate impact on the ratings on Danske Bank  or its subsidiaries. 
The above-mentioned additional Pillar II capital requirement does not impact 
our assessment on Danske Bank 's capital and earnings or risk position. We also 
believe that Danske Bank  will continue to invest in risk management 
improvements. 
 
The positive outlook on Danske Bank  indicates that we could raise our 
long-term ratings by one notch if the bank realizes its issuance plans on 
bail-in-able senior nonpreferred debt throughout 2018, and approaches its 
target for additional loss-absorbing capacity buffers stemming from the 
minimum requirement for own funds and eligible liabilities. 
 
Only a rating committee may determine a rating action and this report does not 
constitute a rating action.

HD *S&PGR Rates Danske Bank's Proposed Sr Nonpreferred Notes 'A-'
WC 2278 words
PD 4 May 2018
ET 05:36
SN Dow Jones Institutional News
SC DJDN
LA English
CY Copyright 2018, Dow Jones & Company, Inc.

LP 

4 May 2018 05:36 ET Press Release: S&PGR Rates Danske Bank's Proposed Sr Nonpreferred Notes 'A-'

TD 

 
 
The following is a press release from S&P Global Ratings: 
 
     -- Following the proposal of a law introducing a senior nonpreferred 
asset class in Denmark, Danish banking group Danske Bank  intends to issue its 
first notes. 
     -- We believe the proposed notes would be subject to conversion or 
write-down in a resolution after junior instruments, but before more senior 
obligations including senior preferred notes. 
     -- A potential bail-in of the proposed note would not cause a default of 
the bank, in our view. 
     -- We are assigning our 'A-' issue rating to the proposed notes. 
     -- The rating is one notch lower than our assessment of Danske Bank 's 
stand-alone credit profile (SACP), owing to our view that the proposed notes 
are subordinated to more senior obligations and do not carry additional 
default risk relative to that represented by the SACP. 
 
MOSCOW (S&P Global Ratings) May 4, 2018--S&P Global Ratings said today that it 
had assigned its 'A-' long-term issue rating to the proposed senior 
nonpreferred notes to be issued by Denmark-based Danske Bank A/S  
(A/Positive/A-1). The rating is subject to our review of the notes' final 
documentation. 
 
On March 14, 2018, the Danish government proposed implementation of the 
changes to the creditor hierarchy as stipulated in the EU's Directive 
2017/2399/EU, and thereby to introduce a senior nonpreferred asset class into 
Danish regulation. The law is expected to enter into force on July 1, 2018, 
but will apply on instruments issued from Jan. 1, 2018. 
 
Until the law enters into force, the proposed notes will rank pari passu with 
other unsubordinated senior unsecured notes, but senior to subordinated 
instruments, such as additional Tier 1 and Tier 2 capital. However, if the 
legislation change occurs as expected, the instruments will start ranking 
junior to existing and future claims of depositors and now also to preferred 
senior bondholders, while continuing to precede subordinated notes. The 
conversion to senior nonpreferred will only occur if the notes qualify as 
eligible liability to meet final minimum requirement for own funds and 
eligible liabilities (MREL). 
 
The notes' position in the updated creditor hierarchy means that conversion or 
write-down of the proposed notes during a resolution will take place only if 
more junior notes and shareholders' equity have been utilized in full to 
absorb losses. 
 
RATING ANALYSIS OF THE PROPOSED NOTES 
The 'A-' rating relies on our analysis of the terms and conditions of the base 
prospectus for the EUR35 billion euro medium-term note (EMTN) program under 
which the notes will be issued. The rating also takes into account our 
assessment of Danske Bank 's stand-alone credit profile (SACP) at 'a', which is 
based on our analysis of the group (see "Bank Hybrid Capital And Nondeferrable 
Subordinated Debt Methodology And Assumptions," published Jan. 29, 2015). 
 
The rating is one notch lower than the SACP assessment, reflecting the 
deduction of one notch for subordination risk, given that Danske Bank 's SACP 
is in the investment-grade category (higher than 'BB+'). This follows our 
approach when an instrument is subordinated to senior unsecured debt, even if 
it is not labeled as subordinated, as we expect to be the case for the 
proposed notes after the introduction of the senior nonpreferred asset class 
into Danish law. In addition, we believe that nonpreferred senior notes would 
be subject to a possible conversion or write-down only in resolution. In 
particular, we are of the view that the proposed notes would be excluded from 
any burden-sharing under state-aid rules. Therefore, we have not applied 
further notching from the SACP because we believe that senior nonpreferred 
notes do not carry any additional default risk relative to that represented by 
the SACP assessment. 
 
In our view, holders of senior nonpreferred notes face a higher default risk 
than holders of senior preferred notes and other senior liabilities, since 
senior nonpreferred notes would be bailed in before more senior creditors in 
the event of a resolution under the EU's bank recovery and resolution 
directive. 
 
ALAC ELIGIBILITY 
It is likely that that we would consider this new instrument as eligible for 
ALAC (additional loss-absorbing capacity) inclusion, provided that authorities 
also consider it eligible for total loss absorbing capacity or MREL purposes. 
 
In our view, the notes meet the conditions for ALAC because we consider 
Denmark to have an effective resolution regime, and the notes' terms and 
conditions meet the following conditions: 
     -- They can be subject to a permanent, full, or partial write-down at the 
start of a resolution; 
     -- A write-down or conversion of the notes in resolution is not an event 
of default and would, in our view, not cause the default of the bank or of 
more senior instruments; and 
     -- Write-down or conversion can be exercised at the discretion of the 
resolution authority after obligations that rank junior to the notes have 
fully absorbed losses. 
 
The proposed notes are expected to be under the regulator's oversight as part 
of the bank's MREL reporting. As a result, to be included in ALAC, the 
remaining term of the notes must be at least 12 months. Our ALAC measure 
excludes instruments maturing within 12-24 months that exceed 0.5% of our 
risk-weighted assets as at the projected calculation date.

HD  Danske Bank goes unpunished
WC 64 words
PD 11 May 2018
SN i
SC IIND
ED 1ST
PG 49
LA English
CY  2018 Johnston Publishing Limited. All rights reserved

LP 

News | From the business pages The Baltic Times

The Financial Supervision Authority (FSA) of Denmark has decided not to punish Danske Bank for enabling money laundering via its Estonian branch. However, the FSA has reprimanded the bank's executive board for not following up on allegations made by a whistle-blower four years ago. Danske Bank is Denmark's largest bank.

HD 1Partner: Danske's leaving to have worse impact on Estonia than thought
WC 288 words
PD 15 May 2018
ET 04:51
SN Baltic Business Daily
SC BALDAI
LA English
CY (c) 2018 Baltic News Service

LP 

TALLINN, May 15, BNS According to managing director of the real estate agency 1Partner Kinnisvara Martin Vahter, the essential leaving of Danske Bank from the Baltic countries will decrease competition and shows that Estonia is not considered an important market.

"In the phase of navel-gazing, we cannot see the big picture and feel glad when something goes wrong for someone. Danske is a large international banking corporation that over the years pumped a considerable amount of finances to Estonia and the price level of those loans was actually favorable," Vahter said in a press release.

TD 

"One market share holder was also lost with the merger of Nordea and DNB and there are once more less nutrients in our pond. In the long perspective, the decrease in competition also impacts an ordinary person applying for a mortgage, who will have less options for asking an offer. Large banks continue to set the terms in Estonia, but luckily, of the local ones, the newcomer Coop also seems to have a wider ambition alongside LHV," Vahter said.

"The reason for Danske's leaving is rather not the money laundering scandal but a wider picture that the Baltics are not seen as an important market and money is pulled out of here," Vahter said.

According to Vahter, the impact of Swedish banks on the Estonian economy will thus increase. "It does not seem that Deutsche Bank or Citigroup will start operating here. If it should go sour on the Swedish real estate market, it will also reach us and there is no plan B," Vahter said.

Tallinn newsroom, +372 610 8815, majandus@bns.ee

Baltic News Service

HD Press Release: Fitch Assigns Danske Bank 's Senior Non-Preferred Notes Final 'A' Rating
WC 1970 words
PD 18 May 2018
ET 04:08
SN Dow Jones Institutional News
SC DJDN
LA English
CY Copyright 2018, Dow Jones & Company, Inc.

LP 

 
 
The following is a press release from Fitch Ratings :

Fitch Ratings -London-18 May 2018: Fitch Ratings has assigned Danske Bank AS 's (Danske ; A/Stable) EUR1.25 billion senior unsecured issue convertible into senior non-preferred debt a final long-term rating of 'A'. The notes are issued under the bank's EUR35 billion euro medium-term note programme. They are initially classed as senior unsecured instruments, but will automatically convert to senior non-preferred notes once the relevant Danish legislation is in place, which we expect will happen on 1 July 2018.

TD 

The introduction of this new debt class does not affect the 'A' long-term rating of Danske 's existing senior debt, which following the expected legislative change will become senior preferred obligations of the bank.

Under its criteria, Fitch requires a high burden of proof to notch senior debt up or down from a bank's Issuer Default Rating (IDR) based on recovery prospects, particularly at high rating levels. This is because the structure of a bank's balance sheet is likely to be very different at the point of failure and default is unlikely to result in liquidation for systemically important banks.

Additionally, Fitch believes the difference in default risk between what eventually will be the senior preferred and senior non-preferred debt will initially be very small until the bank has larger buffers of senior non-preferred and junior debt. Over time, a build-up of senior non-preferred notes in combination with Danske 's qualifying junior debt (QJD) could result in a level of protection for senior preferred notes warranting a long-term rating one notch higher than the bank's Long-Term IDR and senior non-preferred debt ratings.

For the future senior preferred notes to achieve a single-notch uplift, the combined buffer of QJD and senior non-preferred debt would need to exceed our estimate of a 'recapitalisation amount'. This amount is likely to be around the bank's fully phased-in minimum pillar 1 total capital requirement. Fitch estimates that based on end-March 2018 figures but including the new issue, Danske 's combined buffer was equal to about 7% of risk-weighted assets, insufficient for an uplift.

KEY RATING DRIVERS

- The new notes are rated in line with Danske 's Long-Term IDR and existing senior debt rating as Fitch views the probability of default on these as the same as the probability of default of the bank.

These notes will become a new senior non-preferred debt class once the relevant new legislation becomes effective in Denmark. The draft bill was presented to parliament on 14 March 2018. We expect it to be passed in 2Q18 and to come into force on 1 July 2018. It will then apply to all senior notes issued from 1 January 2018 where the contractual language stipulates an automatic conversion to senior non-preferred status, and will effectively make these instruments subordinated to existing senior debt (which will then become senior preferred debt) and senior to subordinated debt. The new senior non-preferred notes can be bailed in before senior preferred liabilities in the event of resolution under the EU's Bank Recovery and Resolution Directive.

RATING SENSITIVITIES

- The rating of the senior unsecured issue convertible into senior non-preferred notes is sensitive to changes in Danske 's Long-Term IDR. The rating is also sensitive to the final relevant Danish legislation being materially different from what Fitch anticipates.

The rating actions are as follows:

ISIN XS1799061558: long-term rating assigned at 'A'

Press release, 22 May 2018 
 
NOT FOR RELEASE, PUBLICATION OR DISTRIBUTION, DIRECTLY OR INDIRECTLY, IN 
THE UNITED STATES, CANADA, JAPAN OR AUSTRALIA OR ANY OTHER JURISDICTION 
IN WHICH THE RELEASE, PUBLICATION OR DISTRIBUTION WOULD BE UNLAWFUL. 
 
Carnegie Investment Bank AB (Carnegie) and Danske Bank A/S, Danmark, 
Sverige Filial (Danske Bank) have been retained by Sunstone Technology 
Ventures Fund II K/S (Sunstone) and Verdane Capital VII K/S 
(Verdane) (together the Sellers) to explore the opportunity to sell 
3,546,171 shares in Boozt AB (publ) (Boozt) (the Placing). 
 
The Sellers currently hold the following number of shares, corresponding 
to the following % of the number of shares and votes in Boozt: 
 
    Sunstone: 3,709,567 shares, 6.58% of the shares and votes 
    Verdane: 4,638,514 shares, 8.23% of the shares and votes 
 
The price per share in the Placing will be determined through an 
accelerated bookbuilding process. The bookbuilding period commences 
today, 22 May 2018, at 17:30 CET and may close at any time on short 
notice. Subject to customary exceptions or obtaining consent from 
Carnegie and Danske Bank, the Sellers have agreed to a lock-up period of 
90 days, in relation to their remaining shares in Boozt. 
 
Carnegie and Danske Bank act as joint bookrunners in connection with the 
Placing. 
 
22 May 2018

HD Press Release: Fitch Affirms Danske Bank AS Mortgage Cover Pool C Covered Bonds at 'AAA'
WC 2444 words
PD 23 May 2018
ET 12:34
SN Dow Jones Institutional News
SC DJDN
LA English
CY Copyright 2018, Dow Jones & Company, Inc.

LP 

 
 
The following is a press release from Fitch Ratings :

Fitch Ratings -London-23 May 2018: Fitch Ratings has affirmed Danske Bank AS 's (Danske , A/Stable/F1) mortgage covered bonds secured by the bank's cover pool C at 'AAA' with a Stable Outlook.

TD 

KEY RATING DRIVERS

- The covered bonds' rating is based on Danske 's Long-Term Issuer Default Rating (IDR) of 'A' and unchanged uplifts as follows: IDR uplift of two notches; payment continuity uplift (PCU) of five notches and recovery uplift of one notch. Also, the 20.4% over-collateralisation (OC) that Fitch gives credit to and which is the lowest nominal OC of the last 12 months, provides more protection than the revised 18.0% 'AAA' breakeven OC for the programme. The latter supports a 'AA+' tested rating on a probability of default basis and a one-notch recovery uplift to 'AAA'. The Stable Outlook on the covered bonds' rating reflects that on Danske and a three-notch buffer against an issuer downgrade, due to the different uplift factors above the bank's IDR.

The increase in the 'AAA' breakeven OC for this programme, to 18.0% from 17.0%, is driven by an increased credit loss component to 17.3% in the 'AA+' stress scenario tested for timely payment. This is due to the higher geographical exposure to commercial real estate in Norway (to 42% on 31 March 2018 from 30% on 31 March 2017).

In its analysis, Fitch applied a benchmark one-year PD of 1.5% for loans secured by Swedish commercial real estate, with a PD floor of 0.5%, compared with 2.25% for loans secured by Norwegian commercial real estate (with a floor at 0.5%). In addition to the larger geographical exposure to Norway, the number of obligors representing more than 50 basis points of the portfolio notional has increased to 27 as of March 2018, from 24 in March 2017. For these obligors Fitch applies a minimum one-year PD of at least 1.0%, a correlation uplift of 50% and a recovery rate multiplier of 0.5, in line with criteria.

Fitch assumed a 40% cure rate in a 'B' scenario. The market value decline (MVD) assumptions were applied according to the SME Balance Sheet Securitisation Rating Criteria, where multi-family properties were treated as residential property in metropolitan areas, while the remaining property types were treated as commercial properties. In assessing the cover pool's PD, Fitch has assumed a three-year longer maturity for the interest-only loans (25%). In the cash flow modelling, a low and high stressed prepayment rate of 5% and 30%, respectively, was applied.

The cash flow valuation component leads to a lower 'AAA' breakeven OC by 0.1% due to positive excess spread on the underlying assets versus the covered bonds in Fitch's worst case high prepayment scenario. The asset disposal loss component increases the breakeven OC by 0.6%, reflecting low maturity mismatches. The weighted average life (WAL) of the assets modelled by Fitch is 3.2 years while the WAL of the covered bonds is 3.1 years.

The programme's two-notch IDR uplift reflects that covered bonds issued by retail banks in Denmark are exempt from bail-in, Fitch's assessment that the risk of under-collateralisation at the point of resolution is sufficiently low, and that a resolution of Danske , should it happen, would not result in the direct enforcement of the recourse against the cover pool.

Fitch's PCU for Danske 's C programme is five notches, rather than the standard six for mortgage covered bonds with a 12-month principal maturity extension and three-month protection for interest payment. This is due to the lack of formal provisions to find a refinancing solution without delay in the event of a maturity extension.

The recovery uplift for this programme is capped at one notch due to the presence of significant pre-swap FX mismatches between cover assets and liabilities. The FX covered bonds are fully hedged until maturity (including the extension period). However, upon a covered bonds' default, recoveries from SEK- and NOK-denominated assets, which have a longer WAL than the covered bonds, could expose holders of non SEK- and non NOK-denominated bonds to FX risk.

RATING SENSITIVITIES

- The 'AAA' rating of Danske Bank AS 's cover pool C mortgage covered bonds would be vulnerable to a downgrade if any of the following occurs: (i) Danske 's Long-Term Issuer Default Rating (IDR) is downgraded by four notches to 'BBB-' or below; or (ii) the payment continuity uplift is reduced to one notch or less; or (iii) the level of overcollateralisation (OC) Fitch gives credit to in its analysis fell below the 'AAA' breakeven OC for the programme of 18.0%. If the actual OC is reduced to the legal minimum of 0%, the covered bonds would be downgraded to 'AA', three notches above the bank's IDR.

The Fitch breakeven OC for the covered bond rating will be affected, among others, by the profile of the cover assets relative to outstanding covered bonds, which can change over time, even in the absence of new issuance. Therefore the breakeven OC to maintain the covered bond rating cannot be assumed to remain stable over time.

SE Economy
HD Quick Hits: San Francisco Fed Says Bitcoin Bears Bubble Trappings; Singapore's central bank gets cracking on cryptocurrencies
BY By WSJ Staff
WC 844 words
PD 24 May 2018
ET 15:25
SN WSJ Pro Central Banking
SC RSTPROCB
LA English
CY Copyright 2018, Dow Jones & Company, Inc.

LP 

The San Francisco Fed says bitcoin's price swings are suggestive of a bubble, Singapore's central bank took steps to regulate cryptocurrencies, and the People's Bank of China is seen easing monetary policy. Here are quick hits on central banking and related market views from around the world.

San Francisco Fed Says Bitcoin Bears Bubble Trappings

TD 

The San Francisco Fed says in new research something a lot of folks have pretty much come to terms with: that the massive run-up in bitcoin was a bubble. In the paper, bitcoin's value is deemed "overpriced" by any conventional metric of proper valuation. What's more, a widely understood way of thinking about financial instability appears to describe bitcoin's price surge and subsequent reversal, with the paper saying, "by now Bitcoin seems to bear mostif not allhallmarks of a bubble."

Michael S. Derby

Singapore Central Bank Gets Cracking on Cryptos

Singapore's central bank is seeking to regulate the issuance and trading of cryptocurrencies, joining others globally looking to at minimum keep that sector penned in. The Monetary Authority of Singapore has warned eight digital-token exchange operators not to facilitate trading without its authorization and an issuer of an initial coin offering to stop the planned sale in Singapore.

Gaurav Raghuvanshi

Trump Auto Tactic Wipes Out Chances of Bank of Canada Rate Rise

The Trump administration's move to consider placing tariffs on imported vehicles and auto parts on national-security grounds has wiped out any chance Bank of Canada raises its benchmark rate Wednesday, says Bank of Nova Scotia economist Derek Holt. Mr. Holt and his firm were among the few economic houses saying the recent string of data could justify an increase on May 30. Uncertainty over U.S. trade policy in terms of the North American Free Trade Agreement has weighed on BOC policy-making.

Paul Vieira

Brazil's External Accounts Bring Relief To Currency

Brazil's balance of payments in April kept bringing relief to an economy facing strong headwinds from global turmoil. The central bank reported Thursday a $620 million current-account surplus for the month, keeping the 12-month deficit at a mere 0.43% of gross domestic product. Brazil's hard-currency reserves reached $380 billion, which the bank said is 3.74 times as high as the external debt coming due in the next 12 months. The currency has been weakening, but economists say good balance of payment results are keeping it from depreciating even more.

Paulo Trevisani

Turkey's Rate Rise a Step to Normalizing Situation: BBVA

The Turkish central bank's actiona 3-percentage-point emergency rate increase Wednesday eveningis an "important step to normalize the situation," say BBVA analysts. They add that the action, and more if needed, should be reinforced in a comprehensive way and elevated at the top of the agenda. This agenda should include monetary and fiscal policy tightening, the removal of distortions in the monetary transmission mechanism, completing foreign-exchange hedge legislation and accepting a lower but healthier growth target, BBVA analysts say.

Emese Bartha

Pressure on Turkish Lira to Remain Until June Elections: Danske Bank

The sizable emergency interest-rate increase by Turkey's central bank late Wednesday will take the pressure off the lira in the near term and improve confidence in the central bank's ability to act, but it still may not be enough to stem selling pressure, says Danske Bank "We think the pressure on the [lira] will remain high until the elections on 24 June. However, we expect another rate hike at the monetary policy meeting on 7 June, if not earlier, should the lira continue to remain under pressure," it says.

Yeliz Candemir

PBOC May Need to Ease More as Uncertainties Rise

Oxford Economics sees the People's Bank of China likely taking quick actions to further ease monetary policy to ensure economic growth amid lingering trade tensions and softening domestic demand. While it thinks Beijing probably won't back away from reining in credit growth and financial risks, a "significantly more-forceful slowdown" in credit growth may endanger the government's 6.5% economic growth target for this year.

Liyan Qi

Slight Uptick in Aussie Inflation May Loom

Citi's Australian economists have fed the bank's new forecasts on oil, currencies and the global economy into their local consumer-price index models and see price growth picking up. It sees CPI rising to 2.2% the rest of the year and being at 2% for all of 2019. That is all consistent with a slow process of monetary policy normalization. By the end of 2019, Citi forecasts a Reserve Bank of Australia cash rate of 2%, which means two quarter-point increases the next 19 months.

James Glynn

HD Handelsbanken: Nordic banks to explore common KYC joint venture
WC 344 words
PD 31 May 2018
ET 02:00
SN Dow Jones Institutional News
SC DJDN
LA English
CY Copyright 2018, Dow Jones & Company, Inc.

LP 

TD 

 
Leading Nordic banks DNB Bank ASA, Danske Bank A/S, Nordea Bank AB 
(publ), Svenska Handelsbanken AB (publ) and Skandinaviska Enskilda 
Banken AB (publ) have decided to explore the possible establishment of a 
Nordic Know Your Customer (KYC) infrastructure that would, in initial 
phase, service large and midsize Nordic corporates. 
 
In recent years, compliance with requirements for processing customer 
data has become a critical component in fighting financial crime. Bank 
customers are, however, struggling with time-consuming KYC information 
requirements, often including many banks and formats. Inefficient KYC 
processes also impact banks negatively, slowing down transaction 
processes, and increasing administration and risks. 
 
At the same time, the banking community is continuously facing more 
regulations and requirements related to KYC processes. There is hence a 
need for a consolidated, efficient and accurate way to serve customers, 
banks and society. 
 
The banks intend to set up a joint venture, Nordic KYC Utility, with a 
singular focus on developing an efficient, common, secure and cost 
-effective Nordic KYC infrastructure. The company will be owned and 
controlled by the founding banks, however, the plan is that the company 
will also offer its services to third parties. The initiative will 
contribute to ensuring a healthy financial environment, prevent 
financial crime and to protect customers and society. 
 
The establishment and operational start of the joint venture company is 
conditional upon approval of the European Commission under the EU Merger 
Regulation and the company is expected to be established during the 
second half of 2018. 
For further information, please contact: 
Mats Olsson, Pressofficer, +46 8701 35 47, +46 70688 07 99 
For more information about Handelsbanken, see: 
www.handelsbanken.com[http://www.handelsbanken.com] (http://www.handelsbanken.se/[http://www.handelsbanken.se/])

HD *Nordic Banks to Explore "Know Your Customer" Infrastructure Joint Venture
WC 303 words
PD 31 May 2018
ET 02:05
SN Dow Jones Institutional News
SC DJDN
LA English
CY Copyright 2018, Dow Jones & Company, Inc.

LP 

31 May 2018 02:05 ET *Nordic Banks JV Would Initially Service Large, Midsize Nordic Companies

31 May 2018 02:07 ET *Nordic Banks JV Aims to Increase Efficiencies Surrounding Financial Crime Regulations

TD 

31 May 2018 02:09 ET *Nordic Banks JV Would Be Called Nordic KYC Utility, Establishment Seen in 2H18

31 May 2018 02:39 ET Nordic Banks Explore 'Know Your Customer' Infrastructure JV

 
   By Dominic Chopping

STOCKHOLM--Nordic banks DNB ASA (DNB.OS), Danske Bank A/S (DANSKE.KO), Nordea Bank AB (NDA.SK), Svenska Handelsbanken AB (SHB-B.SK) and Skandinaviska Enskilda Banken AB (SEB-A.SK) are looking to establish a joint venture aimed at increasing efficiencies surrounding financial crime regulations, according to a joint statement from the banks.

The joint venture, Nordic KYC Utility, would develop an efficient, common, secure and cost-effective Nordic infrastructure to process the so-called "Know Your Customer" regulations designed to fight money laundering.

The company will be owned and controlled by the founding banks, initially servicing large and midsize Nordic corporates.

"In recent years, compliance with requirements for processing customer data has become a critical component in fighting financial crime," the banks said in a joint statement Thursday.

"The banking community is continuously facing more regulations and requirements related to KYC processes. There is hence a need for a consolidated, efficient and accurate way to serve customers, banks and society," they said.

The establishment and operational start of the joint venture is conditional upon approval of the European Commission and the company is expected to be established during the second half of 2018.

-Write to Dominic Chopping at dominic.chopping@wsj.com; Twitter : @domchopping @WSJNordics

(END) Dow Jones Newswires

HD *SEB: Nordic banks to explore common KYC joint venture
WC 511 words
PD 31 May 2018
ET 02:00
SN Dow Jones Institutional News
SC DJDN
LA English
CY Copyright 2018, Dow Jones & Company, Inc.

LP 

31 May 2018 02:00 ET Press Release: SEB: Nordic banks to explore common KYC joint venture

TD 

 
   Leading Nordic banks DNB Bank ASA , Danske Bank A/S , Nordea Bank AB  
(publ), Svenska Handelsbanken AB  (publ) and Skandinaviska Enskilda 
Banken AB  (publ) have decided to explore the possible establishment of a 
Nordic Know Your Customer (KYC) infrastructure that would, in initial 
phase, service large and midsize Nordic corporates. 
 
   In recent years, compliance with requirements for processing customer 
data has become a critical component in fighting financial crime. Bank 
customers are, however, struggling with time-consuming KYC information 
requirements, often including many banks and formats. Inefficient KYC 
processes also impact banks negatively, slowing down transaction 
processes, and increasing administration and risks. 
 
   At the same time, the banking community is continuously facing more 
regulations and requirements related to KYC processes. There is hence a 
need for a consolidated, efficient and accurate way to serve customers, 
banks and society. 
 
   The banks intend to set up a joint venture, Nordic KYC Utility, with a 
singular focus on developing an efficient, common, secure and 
cost-effective Nordic KYC infrastructure. The company will be owned and 
controlled by the founding banks, however, the plan is that the company 
will also offer its services to third parties. The initiative will 
contribute to ensuring a healthy financial environment, prevent 
financial crime and to protect customers and society. 
 
   The establishment and operational start of the joint venture company is 
conditional upon approval of the European Commission  under the EU Merger 
Regulation and the company is expected to be established during the 
second half of 2018. 
 
 
 
 
For further information, please contact 
 Frank Hojem, Head of Media Relations 
 +46 70 763 99 47, frank.hojem@seb.se 
 
SEB is a leading Nordic financial services group with 
 a strong belief that entrepreneurial minds and innovative 
 companies are key in creating a better world. SEB 
 takes a long-term perspective and supports its customers 
 in good times and bad. In Sweden and the Baltic countries, 
 SEB offers financial advice and a wide range of financial 
 services. In Denmark, Finland, Norway, Germany and 
 UK the bank's operations have a strong focus on corporate 
 and investment banking based on a full-service offering 
 to corporate and institutional clients. The international 
 nature of SEB's business is reflected in its presence 
 in some 20 countries worldwide. On March 31, 2018, 
 the Group's total assets amounted to SEK 2,903 billion 
 while its assets under management totalled SEK 1,854 
 billion. The Group has around 15,000 employees. Read 
 more about SEB at  http://www.sebgroup.com [http://www.sebgroup.com]. 
 
 
 
   Press release (PDF):  http://hugin.info/1208/R/2196176/851071.pdf [http://hugin.info/1208/R/2196176/851071.pdf] 
 
   This announcement is distributed by Nasdaq Corporate Solutions on behalf 
of Nasdaq Corporate Solutions clients. 
 
   The issuer of this announcement warrants that they are solely 
responsible for the content, accuracy and originality of the information 
contained therein.

HD Press Release: Aarsleff to construct new headquarters for Danske Bank
WC 219 words
PD 5 June 2018
ET 09:16
SN Dow Jones Institutional News
SC DJDN
LA English
CY Copyright 2018, Dow Jones & Company, Inc.

LP 

TD 

 
                     Per Aarsleff A/S  has entered into a contract with Danica Pension for the 
construction of Danske Bank 's new headquarters at the old post office 
property at Bernstorffsgade in Copenhagen. 
 
   The work has a total building area of approx. 113,000 square metres: 
Danske Bank 's headquarters will occupy 73,000 square metres, and 40,000 
square metres will be used for parking facilities and technical 
installations. 
 
   The contract is carried out as a design and build contract, and the 
Aarsleff Group company Wicotec Kirkebjerg A/S will carry out the 
technical installations. Danica Pension is the client of the project, 
COWI is consulting engineer, and Lundgaard & Tranberg Arkitekter is 
consulting architect. 
 
   The construction activities will begin on 1 June 2019 with completion 
expected in 2023. 
 
   The contract has a value of approx. DKK 3 billion and is a continuation 
of the ongoing contracts for demolition and construction pit. 
 
   The contract does not affect Aarsleff's earnings expectations for the 
financial year 2017/18. 
 
 
 
   Further information: 
 
   General Manager Ebbe Malte Iversen , tel. +45 8744 2222. 
 
   Attachment 
 
 
   -- Aarsleff skal opfre Danske Banks nye hovedsde_UK

   Major shareholder announcement 
 
   Netcompany Group A/S (the "Company" or "Netcompany ") hereby announces 
the following notifications received pursuant to section 38 of the 
Danish Capital Markets Act and the Danish Executive Order on Major 
Shareholders from Danske Bank A/S , regarding their direct and indirect 
holdings in Netcompany . 
 
 
 
   Danske Bank A/S  has today informed the Company, that Danske Bank A/S  as 
of 7 June 2018 directly and indirectly via Danica Pension, 
Livsforsikringsaktieselskab , Danica Pension 
Frskringsaktiebolag, Sweden and Danske  Invest in aggregate 
holds 4,721,431 shares, each with a nominal value of DKK 1 corresponding 
to 9.44% of the total share capital and holds 2,858,930 voting rights 
corresponding to 5.72% of the total voting rights in the Company. 
 
 
 
   FMR LLC , Wilmington USA has today informed the Company, that FMR LLC  as 
of 7 June 2018 indirectly holds 2,695,495 shares and voting rights, each 
with a nominal value of DKK 1, corresponding to 5.39% of the total share 
capital and the total voting rights of the Company. 
 
 
 
   The shares are held directly by (i) FIAM LLC, Fidelity Institutional 
Asset Management Trust Company, which are controlled by FIAM Holdings 
LLC, which in turn is controlled by FMR LLC , (ii) FMR Investment 
Management (UK) Limited, which is controlled by Fidelity Management & 
Research  (U.K.) Inc., which is controlled by Fidelity Management & 
Research Company , which is controlled by FMR LLC , (iii) FMR Co., Inc., 
Fidelity Management & Research  (Japan) Limited, Fidelity Management & 
Research  (Hong Kong) Limited, which are controlled by Fidelity 
Management & Research Company , which is controlled by FMR LLC  and (iv) 
Fidelity Management & Research Company , which is controlled by FMR LLC . 
 
 
 
   Additional information 
 
   For additional information, please contact 
 
   Netcompany Group A/S

TIDMSAMPO 
 
   SAMPO PLC   STOCK EXCHANGE RELEASE   19 June 2018 at 3:50 pm 
 
   Mandatum Life and Danske Bank continue co-operation as agreed 
 
   Mandatum Life Insurance Company Limited (Mandatum Life) disclosed on 24 
April 2018 that Mandatum Life and Danske Bank have agreed to continue 
their co-operation regarding the distribution and management of 
insurance products and the cancellation of the earlier agreed transfer 
of the insurance portfolio distributed by Danske Bank. The agreed 
transaction was subject to confirmation of the tax treatment. 
 
   Mandatum Life received a negative pre-ruling on the tax treatment of the 
transaction on 29 May 2018. However, Mandatum Life and Danske Bank have 
today agreed to continue their co-operation as agreed. 
 
   The parties of the transaction will appeal against the pre-ruling. If 
the tax treatment remains negative, Mandatum Life's financial risk is 
EUR 13 million. 
 
   Danske Bank will pay the agreed transaction price of EUR 197 million by 
the end of June 2018.

SE Economy
HD Quick Hits: Riksbank's Negative Rate Policy Could Backfire, SEB Says; Sweden's central bank also is looking for a new bank note supplier
BY By WSJ Staff
WC 1003 words
PD 19 June 2018
ET 14:41
SN WSJ Pro Central Banking
SC RSTPROCB
LA English
CY Copyright 2018, Dow Jones & Company, Inc.

LP 

Sweden's negative interest rate policy is seen as potentially leading to an "inflation problem," the eurozone's current-account surplus eased further in April, and comments from China's central bank could point to further policy easing. Here are quick hits on central banking and related market views from around the world.

Riksbank's Negative Rate Policy Could Backfire: SEB

TD 

Riksbank keeps pursuing an accommodative monetary policy to reach its inflation target. But negative interest rates have created credit and financial gaps, which Riksbank has to address, says Robert Bergqvist, chief economist at Swedish bank SEB. Otherwise, "financial imbalances will become an inflation problem," he says. Mr. Bergqvist also says that the Riksbank "made huge investments in the inflation target and we have questions about its credibility." The Riksbank aims to keep annual CPIF inflation at around 2%.

Olga Cotaga

Other Central Banks Criticize Riksbank's eKrona Proposal: SEB

The Riksbank has been brainstorming whether it should introduce a virtual currency called eKrona, and other central banks aren't receiving this lightly, says Robert Bergqvist, chief economist at Swedish bank SEB. They are of the opinion that the Riksbank is rushing too quickly into something that could be irreversible, and that the adoption of a virtual currency should be considered very seriously, Mr. Bergqvist says. Virtual money has become a popular topic after bitcoin prices shot higher last year. But Riksbank had been looking at a possible introduction of an eKrona earlier given that Sweden has become an increasingly cashless society.

Olga Cotaga

Sweden's Central Bank Looks for New Bank Note Supplier

Sweden's central bank Tuesday gave notice of termination of its contract with Crane AB, the company that prints Swedish bank notes. Crane will close its bank note printing operations in Tumba, just outside Stockholm, at the end of this year, moving them to its plant on Malta. The Riksbank said that as their agreement with Crane states they will print Swedish bank notes at the printing works in Tumba, the central bank is giving notice of termination of the contract. "The Riksbank is now working on finding a new supplier to manufacture Swedish bank notes," it said. The Riksbank had its own production of both coins and bank notes until the early 2000s, but since 2002 it has procured the manufacture of both bank notes and coins on the international market. Bank notes have been printed in Tumba, while coins have been manufactured abroad since 2008.

Dominic Chopping

Norges Bank Tightening to Mark Next Leg Lower For EUR/NOK: Danske

Danske Bank expects the Norwegian central bank, or Norges Bank, to start raising interest rates in September, which it says marks an important fundamental trigger for lifting the Norwegian krone and sending EUR/NOK on its next leg lower. However, Danske says short-term headwinds such as weaker global growth, a stronger U.S. dollar and improved structural NOK liquidity remain, limiting the potential for near-term EUR/NOK falls.

Dominic Chopping

Eurozone Current-Account Surplus Eases Further

The eurozone's current-account surplus eased further in April, registering its third straight monthly decline, but it remained elevated compared with last April, data from the European Central Bank showed Tuesday. The region's current-account balancea measure of flows in exports and imports, net income from abroad and net current transferseased to 28.4 billion ($33 billion) from a revised surplus of 32.8 billion in March. By comparison, the surplus was 22.9 billion in April last year. The data takes account of seasonal swings and calendar effects. The eurozone's surplus also remained elevated on a 12-month accumulated basis. In the 12 months through April, the eurozone recorded a current-account surplus of 413.7 billion, which equals about 3.7% of its gross domestic product. By comparison, the U.S.'s current-account balance records a deficit.

Nina Adam

PBOC Points to Further Policy Easing

New wording appeared in a People's Bank of China interview with state media, sending a strong message that it likely would introduce easing measures soon, says Nomura economist Ting Lu. He thinks steps will include another full-point cut to reserve-requirement ratios by July, more commercial-bank loan quotas and increased direct funding from the central bank via pledged supplemental lending. In the interview, the PBOC said it would "closely monitor domestic and external economic and financial market trends" and "actively and effectively respond to potential external shocks." The comments came right after U.S. President Donald Trump announced the initial round of trade tariffs on Chinese goods, Mr. Lu noted.

Grace Zhu

PBOC Injects 200 Billion-Yuan Liquidity Via Medium-Term Lending Facility

China's central bank injected 200 billion yuan ($31 billion) in liquidity via its medium-term lending facility on Tuesday, in a bid to meet the long-term fund shortage in the banking system. The People's Bank of China said the one-year MLF carries a 3.3% interest rate, unchanged from its previous operation. The PBOC also injected 100 billion yuan in liquidity via its reverse repo on Tuesday.

Grace Zhu

RBA Prudently' Omits Rate-Path Message

Westpac calls prudent Australia's central bank dropping out of this month's meeting minutes any mention of what the likely next move in interest rates will be. Minutes for the April and May gatherings said up is what's likely to come. The investment bank thinks the Reserve Bank of Australia wants to prevent the market from becoming fixated such statements. RBA Gov. Philip Lowe said as recently as Wednesday that rates most likely will go up next. As such, that "remains the RBA's central case view."

David Winning

(Most of the items in this column come from Market Talk, a feature of Dow Jones Newswires [https://www.dowjones.com/products/newswires/?mod=article_inline&mod=article_inline&mod=article_inline&mod=article_inline&mod=article_inline&mod=article_inline&mod=article_inline&mod=article_inline&mod=article_inline&mod=article_inline&mod=article_inline&mod=article_inline&mod=article_inline] that provides real-time analysis of news developments and market activity.)

HD *S&PGR Assigns Danske Bank 's Proposed AT1 Notes 'BBB-' Rating
WC 1867 words
PD 21 June 2018
ET 07:28
SN Dow Jones Institutional News
SC DJDN
LA English
CY Copyright 2018, Dow Jones & Company, Inc.

LP 

21 Jun 2018 07:28 ET Press Release: S&PGR Assigns Danske Bank 's Proposed AT1 Notes 'BBB-' Rating

TD 

 
 
The following is a press release from S&P Global Ratings: 
 
MOSCOW (S&P Global Ratings) June 21, 2018--S&P Global Ratings said today that 
it has assigned its 'BBB-' long-term issue rating to the perpetual additional 
tier 1 (AT1) capital notes to be issued by Denmark-based Danske Bank A/S  
(A/Positive/A-1). The rating is subject to our review of the notes' final 
documentation. 
 
In accordance with our criteria for rating hybrid capital, our 'BBB-' rating 
on the proposed AT1 notes is four notches below our 'a' assessment of Danske 
Bank 's unsupported group credit profile. This four-notch difference represents: 
     -- One notch to reflect subordination risk. 
     -- Two additional notches to take into account tier 1 regulatory capital 
status. 
     -- One notch to reflect a mandatory contingent capital clause that would 
lead to equity conversion if Danske Bank 's common equity tier 1 (CET1) ratio 
fell below 7%. We consider this a going-concern trigger. 
 
We view risk of conversion as limited for Danske Bank  since its consolidated 
CET1 ratio was 16.4% at March 31, 2018, well above the 11.2% minimum set by 
the regulator and the 7% trigger in the proposed issue. The trigger language 
in the proposed issue additionally references Danske Bank 's stand-alone CET1, 
which was 19.3% on the same date. We expect the CET1 ratios will remain at 
more than 700 basis points above the 7% trigger. 
 
This proposed issuance is neutral for our issuer credit ratings on Danske Bank . 
 
We expect to assign intermediate equity content to the proposed notes since 
they meet our conditions. More specifically, they: 
     -- Are perpetual, with a call date we expect will be five or more years 
from issuance; 
     -- Do not contain a coupon step-up; and 
     -- Have loss-absorption features as a going concern, given that Danske 
Bank  has the flexibility to suspend the coupon at any time. 
 
On April 19, 2018, we published new criteria for assigning resolution 
counterparty ratings (RCRs) to certain financial institutions. We consider 
that there is an effective resolution regime in Denmark, and that an RCR may 
be relevant to Danske Bank  under these criteria. In the coming weeks, we will 
be reviewing our analysis of the resolution regime across 26 countries, 
including Denmark. This review will identify liability categories, if any, 
that are protected from default risk by structural or operational features of 
a given resolution framework. On completion of this review, we may assign RCRs 
under our new criteria to banks located in Denmark, including Danske Bank .

HD Estonia: Iva Pae to step down as head of Baltic banking at Danske Bank
WC 169 words
PD 22 June 2018
ET 08:19
SN Baltic Business Daily
SC BALDAI
LA English
CY (c) 2018 Baltic News Service

LP 

TALLINN, Jun 22, BNS Ivar Pae at the end of June is to leave the position of head of Baltic banking at Danske Bank and will leave the bank.

"Ivar Pae is to be on vacation until fall and will then be open to new challenges," Tonu Talinurm, head of Baltic communications at Danske Bank, told BNS.

TD 

Following a recent decision to bring the Baltic business activity in accordance with the strategy of the group, to remain servicing the subsidiaries of its Nordic customers as well as international corporations, Danske Bank is to change its management structure in the Baltics, Danske said.

As the bank is to exit local business in the Baltics, there will no longer be any need for the position of head of Baltic banking.

Ivar Pae has been working at Danske Bank since 2011, after coming there from Sampo Pank.

Tallinn newsroom, +372 610 8827, majandus@bns.ee

Baltic News Service

HD EUR 7 bln may have been laundered through Estonian branch of Danske Bank
WC 372 words
PD 4 July 2018
ET 06:13
SN Baltic Business Daily
SC BALDAI
LA English
CY (c) 2018 Baltic News Service

LP 

TALLINN, Jul 04, BNS Danske Bank's Estonian operations may have been used to launder as much as 7 billion euros, which is more than twice as much as initially believed and which makes this one of the largest known money laundering incidents in Europe, Bloomberg reports.

The publication said that the amount, which represents roughly a third of Danske's market value and almost 3 percent of Danish gross domestic product (GDP), is more than double that previously estimated, according to figures first reported by Berlingske and confirmed by Bloomberg. The sum also makes up nearly a third of the GDP of Estonia.

TD 

After the latest allegations, Danske's head of group compliance Anders Meinert Jorgensen, said "it is too soon to draw any conclusions about the extent of the potential money laundering in Estonia."

"That is the reason why we have not ourselves published figures or commented on speculations about potential amounts. On several occasions, however, we have said that the extent seems to be somewhat larger than previously estimated," he said.

Danske Bank last September announced it has expanded its ongoing investigation into the customers and transactions of its Estonian branch from 2007 to 2015. The bank hired Jens Madsen, the former head of Denmark's intelligence agency and fraud squad, to help the bank in its effort to investigate a possible case of money laundering in the Estonian branch of the bank.

The bank in October 2017 was placed under investigation by the High Court of Paris in relation to suspicions of money laundering concerning transactions carried out by customers of Danske Bank Estonia from 2008 to 2011. According to the Danish daily Berlingske, the investigation launched by French authorities into the activities of the Estonian branch of Danske Bank is linked to the case of Russian lawyer Sergei Magnitsky.

Danske Bank at the end of April 2018 announced it is about to stop serving local business and private banking customers in the Baltic countries. The group said that the move was in line with their strategy to focus exclusively on supporting subsidiaries of Nordic customers and global corporates "with a significant Nordic footprint."

Baltic News Service

HD  Danske Bank shares fall on money laundering allegations
BY Richard Milne, Nordic and Baltic Correspondent
WC 522 words
PD 4 July 2018
ET 03:54
SN Financial Times (FT.Com)
SC FTCMA
LA English
CY Copyright 2018 The Financial Times Ltd. All rights reserved. Please do not cut and paste FT articles and redistribute by email or post to the web.

LP 

Reported figure of $8.3bn is more than double previous estimates

Shares in Danske Bank fell 3 per cent after reports that it may have laundered up to $8.3bn through its Estonian operations, more than double previous estimates, increasing the pressure on Denmarks biggest bank.

TD 

Danish newspaper Berlingske reported that as much as DKr53bn of suspicious money had flowed through the Estonian branch of Danske.

Rasmus Jarlov, Denmarks business minister, said the gravely serious case was getting worse. It casts a shadow of mistrust over our entire banking system, and nobody gains from that, he wrote on Twitter on Wednesday.

The business minister has said that the banks internal investigation due to report in the autumn might not be sufficient. Opposition lawmakers in Copenhagen have called on Denmarks fraud squad to investigate.

Danske was reprimanded and severely criticised by Danish regulators in May for weak anti-money laundering controls that led to suspected criminal activities involving vast amounts of money. The Danish Financial Supervisory Authority ordered Danske to set aside DKr5bn in capital to cover compliance matters but found insufficient evidence to make a case against any individuals.

The headlines are clearly negative for investor sentiment for Danske, with the [anti-money laundering] issue dragging on stock performance over the past year, said Adam Barrass, analyst at Berenberg, who noted that Danske had underperformed the European banking index by 10 per cent in the past year.

He added that the key risk was a potential US fine because of Danskes use of dollar funding and transactions. But he added that such a fine was unlikely given that Danske has no US banking licence, dollar clearing facility or access to the Federal Reserve liquidity window.

The scandal raises significant questions about what senior management knew, when, and why they failed to act sooner. Danske launched its own investigation last year into the allegations that its Estonian branch was used from 2007 until 2015 for money laundering from countries including Russia, Azerbaijan and Moldova.

The probe could pose questions for Thomas Borgen, Danskes chief executive since 2013, who was in charge of international banking including the Baltics for four years before that.

Anders Jorgensen, head of group compliance at Danske, said it was too early to draw conclusions about the extent of the potential money laundering, meaning that it could not comment on specific figures before its own probe is finished in September.

On several occasions, however, we have said that the extent seems to be somewhat larger than previously estimated...But there is no doubt that even one krone laundered is one too many, and that we take this matter very seriously.

Berlingske said the new transactions it uncovered were linked to the fraud from the Russian treasury discovered by Sergei Magnitsky, a lawyer who was later beaten to death in jail. A French court last year placed Danske under investigation over the Magnitsky case but later dropped the matter.

Danskes shares were down 3 per cent at DKr195 at midday on Wednesday.

HD Danske: Scandi noir
WC 359 words
PD 4 July 2018
ET 13:06
SN Financial Times (FT.Com)
SC FTCMA
LA English
CY Copyright 2018 The Financial Times Ltd. All rights reserved. Please do not cut and paste FT articles and redistribute by email or post to the web.

LP 

Things are looking dark and they could grow darker

A dark cloud hangs over Danske Bank. It would be a fit case for the detectives of a Scandinavian crime drama, if they specialised in forensic accounting alongside homicide. Denmarks biggest bank allegedly laundered money involved in the Magnitsky Case. The eponymous lawyer, who died in Russian police custody, exposed thefts of tax money by gangsters and officials.

TD 

A French court began investigating Danskes Estonian unit last year. On Wednesday, the Berlingske newspaper claimed up to DKr53bn ($8.3bn) was involved, double the original estimate.

This is embarrassing for Danske. Does it matter to investors?

Scandinavias banks are the best of a bad lot in the impaired EU. Danske is no exception. Its co-ordinates could make Italian bankers weep into their Chianti. Last year, core tier one equity was 17.6 per cent, return on equity was 13.6 per cent and loan impairments were 3.5 per cent of pre-tax profits.

Danske is fattening returns with a push into Swedish mortgages. Growth here was a healthy 17 per cent in Danskes first quarter. At 1.2 times tangible book value they trade in line with rival Nordea.

Shares have lagged behind peers by 4 per cent since the French court intervened. But a 2 per cent drop on the day was too muted a response to a doubling in Danskes alleged exposure to money laundering.

Jefferies previously anticipated a provision of DKr2bn, a tenth of net interest income. Nervous Nellies should multiply this by two. You could pick a higher multiplier. BNP Paribas was fined $8.8bn for facilitating money laundering in 2014. HSBC stumped up $1.9bn in 2012.

To the wild card of legal and regulatory action may be added the destabilisation of Danskes management. Opportunists should wait in case sharper price drops afflict a business that otherwise looks sound. This narrative could easily take a gloomier turn.

The Lex team is interested in hearing more from readers. Should we be more positive on Danske? Please tell us what you think in the comments section below.

HD BREAKINGVIEWS-Danske cash gusher faces regulatory blockage
WC 593 words
PD 4 July 2018
ET 08:15
SN Reuters News
SC LBA
LA English
CY Copyright 2018 Thomson Reuters. All Rights Reserved.

LP 

(The author is a Reuters Breakingviews columnist. The opinions expressed are his own.)

By Christopher Thompson

TD 

LONDON, July 4 (Reuters Breakingviews) - Strong and stable with bumper payouts such are the virtues of Nordic lenders embodied by Denmarks Danske Bank. The fallout from a money-laundering scandal involving the banks Estonian branch could cause at least one of those selling points to take a knock.

On Tuesday Berlingske, a local Danish newspaper, reported that Danske had potentially helped launder 53 billion Danish crowns ($8.3 billion) via its Estonian business. Thats roughly double the previous estimate, which first surfaced in March. The lender had already announced that it was investigating suspicious transactions between 2007 and 2015, focusing on non-residents, some of whom were Russian. It also admitted to lax money-laundering controls during the period.

If the money laundering is proven, the size of the potential fine may hinge on whether or not the transactions involved U.S. dollars, dragging U.S. regulators into the fray, as well as Danish ones. Last year, Deutsche Bank agreed to pay $630 million in fines for organising $10 billion in trades that could have been used to launder money out of Russia.

A modest fine shouldnt hurt Danske too much. Jeffries analysts estimates a penalty of around 2 billion Danish crowns, based on previous fines. That would reduce Danskes projected 2018 return on tangible equity from 13 percent to 12 percent, using analysts forecasts available on Eikon. It could still pay the 10.75 Danish crown dividend per share that analysts are expecting merely by raising its payout ratio to 55 percent of earnings, below its 60 percent upper target threshold.

The market, however, seems more nervous. Danskes market capitalisation fell by 8 billion Danish crowns in mid-March, when news of the money laundering started to gather pace. An 8 billion Danish crown fine would drag Danskes leverage ratio down to 4 percent, according to Breakingviews estimates. Thats still above the 3 percent minimum threshold that regulators demand, but probably the lowest level that investors like to see. That may make it hard for the bank to buy back shares or boost lending in Norway and Sweden, as it has promised.

Danske shares fell a further 3 percent on Wednesday. Its shares now yield a whopping 11 percent, including both the expected dividend this year and share buyback, suggesting the market is braced for a harsh outcome.

On Twitter https://twitter.com/CGAThompson [https://twitter.com/CGAThompson]

CONTEXT NEWS

- Danske Bank's Estonian branch was a conduit for suspicious money flows worth at least 53 billion Danish crowns ($8.3 billion), Danish daily newspaper Berlingske said on July 3, citing a leak of bank data.

- Berlingske says it is in possession of bank statements for 20 companies which held accounts with Danskes Estonian branch over various periods from 2007 to 2015, according to a Reuters report on July 3.

- The documents allegedly show some 28 billion Danish crowns being moved through the 20 accounts. That comes on top of money laundering of at least 25 billion Danish crowns through accounts held at the bank's Estonian branch uncovered by Berlingske earlier, the newspaper said.

- Danske Bank shares declined by 3 percent to 195 Danish crowns by 0900 GMT.

Danske Bank  redelivers the shares borrowed according to the share 
lending agreement to Sentica Buyout V Ky and Sentica Buyout V 
Co-Investment Ky. 905,822 new shares offered in accordance with the 
Over-allotment Option will be registered in the Trade Register on or 
about July 6, 2018 and the trading of the new shares will commence on 
First North Finland market place maintained by Nasdaq Helsinki Ltd on or 
about July 9, 2018.

proceeds from the Offering are approximately EUR 34.5 million.

in Estonia and Romania. VMP group operates under VMP Varamiespalvelu , 
Staffplus, Personnel, Romana Management, Eezy and Alina brands.

SE Business
HD  Danske Bank's Baltic scandal deepens
BY RICHARD MILNE
WC 495 words
PD 5 July 2018
SN Financial Times
SC FTFTA
ED 1; Asia
PG 12
LA English
CY Copyright 2018 The Financial Times Ltd. All rights reserved. Please do not cut and paste FT articles and redistribute by email or post to the web.

LP 

Financials Up to $8.3bn said to have been laundered via Estonia double previous estimate

Shares in Danske Bank closed down 2 per cent after reports that it might have laundered up to $8.3bn through its Estonian operations, more than double previous estimates.

TD 

Danish newspaper Berlingske reported that as much as DKr53bn of suspicious money had flowed through the Estonian branch of Danske.

Rasmus Jarlov, business minister, said the "gravely serious" case was getting worse. "It casts a shadow of mistrust over our entire banking system, and nobody gains from that," he tweeted.

The business minister has said that the bank's internal investigation due to report in the autumn might not be sufficient. Opposition lawmakers in Copenhagen have called on the fraud squad to investigate.

Danske was reprimanded and severely criticised by Danish regulators in May for weak laundering controls that led to suspected "criminal activities involving vast amounts of money".

The Danish Financial Supervisory Authority ordered Danske to set aside DKr5bn in capital to cover compliance matters, but found insufficient evidence to make a case against any individuals.

"The headlines are clearly negative for investor sentiment for Danske, with the [money-laundering] issue dragging on stock performance over the past year," said Adam Barrass, analyst at Berenberg, who noted that Danske had underperformed the European banking index by 10 per cent in the past year.

A potential US fine because of Danske's use of dollar funding and transactions was a risk. But such a fine was unlikely given that Danske had no US banking licence, dollar clearing facility or access to the Fed liquidity window.

The scandal raises questions about what management knew, when, and why they failed to act sooner. Danske launched its own probe last year into the allegations that its Estonian branch was used from 2007 until 2015 for moneylaundering from countries including Russia, Azerbaijan and Moldova.

The probe might pose questions for Thomas Borgen, Danske's chief executive since 2013, who was in charge of international banking including the Baltics for four years before that.

Anders Jorgensen, head of group compliance at Danske, said it was too early to draw conclusions about the extent of the potential money-laundering, meaning that it could not comment on specific figures before its own probe finished in September.

"On several occasions, however, we have said that the extent seems to be somewhat larger than previously estimated ... But there is no doubt that even one krone laundered is one too many, and we take this matter very seriously."

Berlingske said the new transactions it had uncovered were linked to the fraud from the Russian treasury discovered by Sergei Magnitsky, a lawyer who was later beaten to death in jail. A French court last year placed Danske under investigation over the Magnitsky case, but later dropped the matter.

HD Press Release: Change in AS Tallink Grupp 's loan obligations
WC 192 words
PD 5 July 2018
ET 09:34
SN Dow Jones Institutional News
SC DJDN
LA English
CY Copyright 2018, Dow Jones & Company, Inc.

LP 

TD 

 
   Today AS Tallink Grupp  signed a loan agreement in the amount of EUR 110 
million. The financing is arranged by Nordea Bank AB  (publ), Finnish 
Branch, Danske Bank A/S , Finland Branch and HSH Nordbank AG . The 
payment- and security agent is Nordea Bank AB  (publ), Finnish Branch. 
The final maturity of the floating interest rate euribor based loan is 
six years. 
 
   The loan will be drawn in October 2018 and proceeds are used to repay 
the NOK 900 million bonds issued in June 2013 and to terminate the 
related hedge transactions. As a result of the transaction Group's 
refinancing risk decreases. 
 
   The new loan is guaranteed by Tallink Fast Ltd., a subsidiary of AS 
Tallink Grupp  and is secured by the mortgage on the vessel Baltic 
Princess belonging to the same subsidiary.

HD Press Release: Major shareholder announcement
WC 426 words
PD 6 July 2018
ET 07:03

SC DJDN
LA English

                     Orphazyme A/S  
 
   Company announcement 
 
 
   No. 09/2018 
 
 
   Company Registration No. 32266355 
 
   Copenhagen, July 6, 2018 -- Orphazyme A/S  (the "Company"), a 
biopharmaceutical company dedicated to developing treatments for 
patients living with rare diseases, hereby announces the receipt of 
notification pursuant to Section 38 of the Danish Capital Markets Act 
from Danske Bank A/S  that its indirect shareholding in the Company is 
1,029,081 shares corresponding to 3.28% of the share capital in the 
Company and that Danske Bank A/S  indirectly has control over 5.16% of 
the voting rights in the Company. 
 
   For additional information, please contact 
 
   Orphazyme  
 
   Anders Vadsholt, CFO                                                         +45 28 98 90 55 
 
 
   About Orphazyme A/S  
 
                     Orphazyme  is a biopharmaceutical company focused on bringing novel 
treatments to patients living with life-threatening or debilitating rare 
diseases. Our research focuses on developing therapies for diseases 
caused by misfolding of proteins, including lysosomal storage diseases. 
Arimoclomol, the company's lead candidate, is in clinical development 
for four orphan diseases: Niemann-Pick disease Type C, Gaucher disease, 
sporadic Inclusion Body Myositis, and Amyotrophic Lateral Sclerosis. The 
Denmark-based company is listed on Nasdaq  Copenhagen (ORPHA.CO). For 
more information, please visit www.orphazyme.com.
